<b>4:15-16 </b>(<b>9</b>:1-2); <b>12:18-21</b> (42:1-4); <b>13:14 </b>(<b>6</b>:9-10);
<b>Luke 3:4-6</b> (<b>40</b>:3-5); <b>John 1:23</b> (<b>40</b>:3); <b>12:38</b>
(53:1); <b>Acts 9:27</b> (<b>10</b>:22-23); <b>10:20 </b>(<b>65</b>:1); and <b>15:12</b>
(<b>11</b>:10). So Isaiah is cited personally only in the historical section of
the New Testament. Jeremiah is named this way in Matthew <b>2</b>:18 (&lt; <b>31</b>:15).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>            <span style='position:relative;top:-3.0pt'>61</span>The
other passages that do not specify the person prophesying are <b>Matthew 2:5-6</b>
(Micah <b>5</b>:2), <b>2:23</b> (Isaiah <b>11</b>:1 in the Hebrew?); <b>13:35</b>
(Psalm <b>78</b>:2); <b>21:5</b> (Isaiah <b>62</b>:11 + Zechariah <b>9</b>:9); <b>24:15</b>
(Daniel <b>9</b>:27; <b>11</b>:31; <b>12</b>:11); <b>Acts 7:49-50</b> (Isaiah<b>
66</b>:1-2); <b>Hebrews 2:6-8</b> (Psalm <b>8</b>:4-6); and <b>7:17</b> (Psalm <b>110</b>:4).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>            <span style='position:relative;top:-3.0pt'>62</span>Paul
quotes Genesis <b>12</b>:3. A similar passage is Romans <b>9</b>:17 (Exodus <b>9</b>:16).
The other predictive prophecies with no mention of personal authorship are
these: <b>Matthew 11:10</b> (Malachi <b>3</b>:1); <b>21:42</b> (Psalm <b>118</b>:22-23);
<b>26:31</b> (Zechariah <b>13</b>:7); <b>Mark 12:10-11</b> (Psalm<b> 118</b>:22-23);
<b>Luke 4:18-19</b> (Isaiah<b> 56</b>:1-2); <b>7:27</b> (Malachi<b> 3</b>:1); <b>20:17</b>
(Psalm<b> 118</b>:22); <b>22:37</b> (Isaiah <b>53</b>:12); <b>6:45</b> (Isaiah <b>54</b>:13);
<b>John 7:42</b> (2 Samuel <b>7</b>:12ff., Micah <b>5</b>:2); <b>10</b>:34 (Psalm<b>
82</b>:6); <b>12:15</b> (Zechariah <b>9</b>:9); <b>13:18 </b>(Psalm <b>41</b>:9);
<b>15:25</b> (Psalm <b>35</b>:19; <b>69</b>:4); <b>17:12</b> (Psalm <b>41</b>:9);
<b>19:24 </b>(Psalm <b>22</b>:18); <b>19:28 </b>(Psalm <b>69</b>:21); <b>19:36</b>
(Exodus <b>12</b>:46; Numbers <b>9</b>:12; Psalm <b>34</b>:20); <b>19:37</b> (Zechariah
<b>12</b>:10); <b>Acts 1:20</b> (Psalm<b> 69</b>:25 + <b>109</b>:8); <b>4:11</b>
(Psalm <b>118</b>:22); <b>7:42-43</b> (Amos <b>5</b>:25-27); <b>8:32-33</b>
(Isaiah <b>53</b>:7-8); <b>13:33</b> (Psalm <b>2</b>:7); <b>13:41</b> (Habakkuk<b>
1</b>:5); <b>13:16-18</b> (Amos <b>9</b>:11-12); <b>Romans 4:17</b> (Genesis <b>17</b>:5);
<b>9:33</b> (Isaiah <b>28</b>:16); <b>10:5-6 </b>(Deuteronomy <b>30</b>:12-14);
<b>10:11</b> (Isaiah <b>28</b>:16);<b> 10:13 (Joel 2:32); 10:18 (Psalm 29:4);
11:26-27 (Isaiah 59:20-21); 14:11 (Isaiah</b> <b>45</b>:23); <b>15:3 </b>(Psalm
<b>59</b>:9); <b>15:9</b> (Psalm <b>18</b>:49); <b>15:21</b> (Isaiah <b>52</b>:15);
<b>1 Corinthians 4:9</b> (Isaiah<b> 64</b>:4 + <b>65</b>:17); <b>14:21</b>
(Isaiah <b>28</b>:11-12); <b>Galatians 4:27</b> (Isaiah <b>54</b>:1); <b>Hebrews
7:17</b> (Psalm <b>110</b>:4); and <b>James 4:6</b> (Proverbs<b> 3</b>:34).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>            <span style='position:relative;top:-3.0pt'>63</span>Cp.
2 Timothy <b>3</b>:16, where the adjective <i>inspired-of-God</i> is literally <i>God-breathed</i>.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>            <span style='position:relative;top:-3.0pt'>64</span>Adam
is not the speaker here since the words are in the form of an injunction.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>            <span style='position:relative;top:-3.0pt'>65</span>For
those passages which credit God with the words of the Old Testament (whether
given there as His words or not), see the following:</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>                  (a)     Lord commanded: Acts <b>13</b>:47.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>                  (b)    Commandment(s) of God/Lord: Matthew
<b>15</b>:3; Mark <b>7</b>:8, 9; 1 Corinthians </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>                           <b>7</b>:19; Romans<b> 16</b>:26.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:99.0pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:-81.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>                  (c)     God/Lord said: 2 Corinthians
<b>4</b>:6; Matthew <b>15</b>:4, 7-9; <b>22</b>:31, 32; Mark <b>12</b>:26; Luke
<b>11</b>:49;<b> 20</b>:37; Acts <b>2</b>:17 (“<i>says</i>” is not in Joel); <b>7</b>:32;
1 Corinthians <b>6</b>:16; 2 Corinthians <b>6</b>:16.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>                  (d)    Oracles of God: Acts<b> 7</b>:38;
Romans <b>3</b>:2; Hebrews<b> 5</b>:12; 1 Peter <b>4</b>:11.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>                  (e)     God-breathed: 2 Timothy <b>3</b>:16.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>                  (f)     Word(s) of God: Matthew <b>15</b>:6;
Mark <b>7</b>:13; Matthew <b>19</b>:4, 5.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>            <span style='position:relative;top:-3.0pt'>66</span>A
confirmatory observation concerning the divine origin of the Old Testament
comes from the use of the word <i>through</i> in citing the prophets’ words. The
implication is that the ultimate origin of the message lay beyond the prophet
through whom it was given. There are instances where <i>through</i> occurs with
God himself (Hebrews <b>2</b>:10). Although this word is sometimes used of the
author of the action, it is most naturally used of the instrument of the
action. Matthew<b> 1</b>:22, <i>“Now all this is come to pass, that it might be
fulfilled which was spoken by the Lord through the prophet,”</i> specifies the
author and then says “through” of the instrument.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>            <span style='position:relative;top:-3.0pt'>67</span>See
“Revelation and Inspiration: Summary Outline” by George Mark Elliott
(unpublished class notes, Cincinnati Christian University, Cincinnati), p. 91.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>            <span style='position:relative;top:-3.0pt'>68</span>See
page <b>13</b>:12.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>            <span style='position:relative;top:-3.0pt'>69</span>A
line of demarcation is difficult to draw between direct assertion and logical
implication. Passages attributed to God we listed last under logical
implication. They dealt with revelation. Since the Holy Spirit is the agent of
inspiration, texts that attribute Old Testament passages to him we list here;
the ones that quote with rubrics like <i>God said </i>and<i> the Lord commanded
</i>we placed under revelation. The distinction between revelation and
inspiration is more theoretical than real, because revelation implies
inspiration since revelation must be preserved without loss or error in order
to serve its purpose. Likewise, inspiration includes revelation.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>            <span style='position:relative;top:-3.0pt'>70</span>Acts
<b>1</b>:16-20 (Psalm<b> 69</b>:25 +<b> 109</b>:8).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>            <span style='position:relative;top:-3.0pt'>71</span>Other
such passages are <b>Matthew 22:43-44 and Mark</b> <b>12:36</b> (Psalm <b>110</b>:1);
<b>Acts 4:25-26</b> (Psalm <b>2</b>:1-2); <b>28:25-27</b> (Isaiah <b>6</b>:9-10)
as well as the general reference 1 Peter <b>1</b>:10-12.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>            <span style='position:relative;top:-3.0pt'>72</span><b>Hebrews
3:7-11</b> (Psalm <b>95</b>:7-11). See also <b>10:15-17</b> (Jeremiah<b> 31</b>:33a,
34b) as well as the general reference in <b>9</b>:8.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>            <span style='position:relative;top:-3.0pt'>73</span>For
further discussion on the interpretation of 2 Peter <b>1</b>:16-21, see endnote
54 and the text to which it is attached.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>            <span style='position:relative;top:-3.0pt'>74</span>See
pp. 1-5.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>            <span style='position:relative;top:-3.0pt'>75</span>See
pp. 5-6.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>            <span style='position:relative;top:-3.0pt'>76</span>See
William Henry Green, <i>op</i>. <i>cit</i>., p. 143, and Westcott and Hort, <i>op</i>.
<i>cit</i>., pp. 601-618. Only Ruth, Ezra, and Lamentations are definitely not
cited. But Ruth being attached to Judges is approved along with Lamentations,
which went with Jeremiah, and Ezra, which accompanied Nehemiah.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>            <span style='position:relative;top:-3.0pt'>77</span>The
quotation as given here follows the American Standard Version with the
exception of the first two commas and the omission of <i>also</i> after <i>is</i>.
The commas are inserted after the current practice of punctuating
non-restrictive elements; the <i>also</i> is omitted because it is not
represented in the Greek. That this participial phrase is non-restrictive is
obvious first from the form of Paul’s argument: the profitableness for the
purposes he specifies comes as a consequence of inspiration. Secondly,
scripture is equated with the sacred writings of verse 15. Being equated with
the sacred writings, “every scripture” must equal the canon of the Jews, whose
limits, as determined at the beginning of this study, are the same as the
thirty-nine books of the modern Old Testament. Furthermore, Paul would not be
helping matters much if he did not proceed to specify which scriptures he had
in mind. <i>Scripture</i> is a quasi-technical term used for the canon of the
Jews. To say <i>“Every scripture that is inspired . . .”</i> is to say that
some of the Old Testament is not inspired. Had Paul said that, he would have
destroyed the purpose of his own teaching, reproof, correction, and instruction
in righteousness.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>            The only way this element could be
considered restrictive is to translate </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:
12.0pt'>γραφή</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt'> </span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>as “writing”: <i>“Every writing that is
inspired-of-God is profitable</i> (others are not).<i>”</i> But the constant
use of the word as a name for the Old Testament makes it unlikely that Paul
would have used it here in such a general way.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>            <span style='position:relative;top:-3.0pt'>78</span>See
the treatment given by Abraham Kuyper in <i>Principles of Sacred Theology</i>,
trans. J. Hendrik De Vries (Grand Rapids: Wm. B. Eerdmans Publishing Company,
1965), p. 432.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>______________</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>                  *Adapted from Dr. Warren’s Th.B.
paper (Cincinnati Christian University), 1968.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>
